Opening Praise and the Foundation of Tawhid
Author opens with praise and introduces the science of tawhid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's opening doxology, the supreme importance of 'ilm al-tawhid as the foundation of all sciences, and the distinction between the immutable creed of tawhid and the changeable religious laws.

Core Idea
Tawhid is the unchanging core of all divine messages; laws may vary, but the creed of God's oneness is eternal.

This lesson presents the opening of Sharh al-Maqasid, where the author begins with praise and then introduces the science of tawhid. He emphasizes that while specific religious laws can change according to circumstances, the fundamental belief in God's oneness remains constant across all prophetic missions. Understanding this distinction is crucial for studying kalam.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening doxology
Read the basmala and hamdalah carefully, noting the attributes of Allah mentioned. This sets the tone for the book.
The author uses names like الواحد الأحد, الفرد الصمد to emphasize tawhid.
2
Identify the claim about tawhid
Find the statement that 'ilm al-tawhid is the foundation of all sciences. Reflect on why the author says this.
This establishes the importance of the subject for the entire work.
3
Distinguish creed and law
Observe the contrast between the unchanging creed of tawhid and the changing laws. Note the Quranic verse quoted.
The Quranic verse (5:48) supports the idea that laws vary among nations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم. الحمد لله الواحد الأحد، الفرد الصمد الذي لم يتخذ صاحبة ولا ولداً. ولم يشاركه في ملكه أحد. يا من تعالت أسماؤك، وتقدست صفاتك. تعطي وتمنع، لا مانع لما أعطيت ولا معطي لما منعت، يا مالك الملك، تعطي من تشاء وتنزع ممن تشاء. والصلاة والتسليم على من اصطفيته من الملك لخير رسالة، وأنزلت عليه خير كتاب لخير أمة أخرجت للناس، سيدنا محمد ابن عبد الله، خاتم الأنبياء والمرسلين، وعلى آله وصحبه، ومن سار على نهجه إلى يوم الدين. وبعد: فإن علم التوحيد، علم جليل الشأن عظيم القدر، شرف بنسبته إلى الله سبحانه تعالى، وهو أساس لكل علم نافع ومفيد. وعقيدة توحيد الله وانفراده باستحقاق الربوبية والمعبودية، جاء أمر الله بها، لكل رسول بعث إلى قومه ليبلغهم باعتناقها لا يعتريها تغيير، ولا تبديل مهما تغيرت الأجيال والأزمان. أما الشرائع المبنية عليها، فإنها تتغير بما يناسب حال كل أمة مصداقاً لقوله تعالى: (لكل جعلنا منكم شرعة ومنهاجا) (سورة المائدة: ٤٨). ولما اكتمل رشد الإنسانية واتسعت دائرة تفكيرها ومواهبها جاءت خاتمة الرسالات، متضمنة شريعة سمحاء لكل زمان ومكان لما اشتملت عليه من المبادئ العامة، وأمهات الفضائل، ولما فيها من سعادة البشرية دنيا وديناً، مع يسرها وعدم الحرج.
In the name of God, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Praise be to God, the One, the Unique, the Individual, the Eternal, who has not taken a companion nor a child. And no one shares with Him in His dominion. O You whose names are exalted, and whose attributes are sanctified. You give and withhold, there is none to prevent what You give nor to give what You withhold. O Possessor of the Kingdom, You give to whom You will and take away from whom You will. And blessings and peace be upon the one whom You chose from the kingdom for the best message, and You sent down upon him the best book for the best nation brought forth for mankind, our master Muhammad ibn Abdullah, the seal of the prophets and messengers, and upon his family and companions, and those who follow his path until the Day of Judgment. And thereafter: The science of tawhid (توحيد) is a science of great status and immense importance, honored by its relation to God Almighty, and it is the foundation of every beneficial and useful science. The creed of tawhid of God and His exclusivity in deserving lordship (ربوبية) and divinity (معبودية) – God's command came with it for every messenger sent to his people to convey to them its adoption; it is not subject to change or alteration no matter how generations and times change. As for the laws (شرائع) built upon it, they change according to what suits the condition of every nation, in confirmation of His saying: (For each of you We have made a law and a pathway) (Surah Al-Ma'idah: 48). And when humanity's maturity was complete and the circle of its thinking and talents expanded, the final message came, containing a tolerant law for every time and place, because it contains general principles and chief virtues, and because it contains happiness for humanity in this world and in religion, along with its ease and absence of hardship.
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This passage is an opening doxology and introduction to the book. The author begins with the basmalah and hamdalah, praising God using names that emphasize His oneness and uniqueness (الواحد الأحد, الفرد الصمد). He then sends blessings upon the Prophet Muhammad, describing him as the chosen one for the best message and the receiver of the best book for the best nation. This is a traditional opening. Then 'Wa ba'd' signals the main introduction. The author states that 'ilm al-tawhid (the science of God's oneness) is a noble science of great standing, honored by its relation to God, and it is the foundation (أساس) of every beneficial and useful science. This establishes the importance of the subject. Next, he explains that the creed of tawhid (that God alone is deserving of lordship and worship) is a universal message that came with every prophet; it never changes or alters regardless of time or place. This guards against the misunderstanding that religious truth changes. In contrast, the specific laws (shara'i') built upon this creed can change according to the circumstances of each nation, as indicated by Quran 5:48. The author then notes that with the completion of human development, the final message (Islam) came, containing a tolerant (samha') law suitable for all times and places, encompassing general principles and chief virtues, bringing happiness in this world and the next, with ease (yusr) and absence of hardship (haraj). Thus, the passage sets the stage for the book by affirming the unchanging core of tawhid and the adaptable nature of its derived laws, with Islam as the final and comprehensive revelation.

Key Terms
توحيد
ربوبية
معبودية
شرائع
شريعة سمحاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The creed of tawhid changes with different religions.
Correction: The author clarifies that the creed of tawhid – affirming God's oneness and exclusive right to worship – remains unchanged across all prophetic missions. Only the specific laws derived from it may vary.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what remains unchanged across all prophetic messages?
A) The specific laws (شرائع)
B) The creed of tawhid (عقيدة التوحيد)
C) The languages of revelation
D) The time periods of messengers

Key Takeaway
The creed of tawhid is the unchanging foundation of all divine religions, while specific laws are adaptable to time and place.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This passage declares that tawhid is the unchanging foundation of every message from God. Yet many of us allow the trends and opinions of our time to quietly reshape how we think about God. Where in your life have you let cultural or personal preferences dilute the pure tawhid that the prophets taught? What concrete step will you take this week to restore that clarity in your heart?
?
The author says the final law came with ease and absence of hardship. But do you find yourself making your religion hard—adding burdens that God did not put, or judging others harshly? Examine your daily practice: is there an area where you can embrace the samha (tolerance) of this sharia, trusting that His way is merciful?
?
The creed of tawhid is the same for all messengers, yet we often treat our own understanding as if it were final and perfect. Are you open to correcting any mistaken beliefs you may hold about God, even if they feel comfortable? Would you be willing to honestly compare your current concept of tawhid with what the prophets actually taught, and change if needed?

Method of Learning

The Dignity of Tawhid and its Unchanging Creed
The editor praises tawhid and explains the fixity of creed vs. change of laws.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the science of tawhid is considered noble and how its core creed remains unchanged while subsidiary laws may vary across nations.

Core Idea
The creed of tawhid is unchanging; laws change, but Islam is the final perfect law.

This passage from the editor's introduction establishes the foundational importance of the science of tawhid. It explains that while the essential belief in Allah's oneness never changes, the legal systems built upon it were tailored to different communities. The final revelation of Islam is presented as the complete and eternal law for all humanity.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening praise
Notice the traditional Islamic opening praising Allah and His Prophet. This sets the tone for the subject's sanctity.
2
Identify the dignity of tawhid
The editor states that the science of tawhid is great in status because it relates to Allah and is the foundation of all useful knowledge.
This is the central claim of the passage.
3
Distinguish creed from law
Understand that the creed (belief in Allah's oneness) is fixed and unchanging, whereas the laws (sharia) varied among prophets and nations. Islam's law is final and perfect.
This distinction is crucial for understanding Islamic theology.
4
Reflect on the unchanging nature
Consider why the creed must be unchanging and how the editor supports this with Quranic verses.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم
الحمد لله الواحد الأحد، الفرد الصمد الذي لم يتخذ صاحبة ولا ولداً. ولم يشاركه في ملكه أحد يا من تعالت أسماؤك، وتقدست صفاتك. تعطي وتمنع، لا مانع لما أعطيت ولا معطي لما منعت، يا مالك الملك، تعطي تشاء وتنزع ممن تشاء، والصلاة والتسليم على من اصطفيته من الملك لخير رسالة، وأنزلت عليه خير كتاب لخير أمة أخرجت للناس، سيدنا محمد ابن عبد الله، خاتم الأنبياء والمرسلين، وعلى آله وصحبه، ومن سار على نهجه إلى يوم الدين .
وبعد
فإن علم التوحيد، علم جليل الشأن عظيم القدر، شرف بنسبته إلى الله سبحانه تعالى، وهو أساس لكل علم نافع ومفيد .
وعقيدة توحيد الله وانفراده باستحقاق الربوبية والمعبودية، جاء أمر الله بها، لكل رسول بعث إلى قومه ليبلغهم باعتناقها لا يعتريها تغيير، ولا تبديل مهما تغيرت الأجيال والأزمان. أما الشرائع المبنية عليها، فإنها تتغير بما يناسب حال كل أمة مصداقاً لقوله تعالى {لكل جعلنا منكم شرعة ومنهاجا} (1) ولما اكتمل رشد الإنسانية واتسعت دائرة تفكيرها ومواهبها جاءت خاتمة الرسالات، متضمنة شريعة سمحاء لكل زمان ومكان لما اشتملت عليه من المبادىء العامة، وأمهات الفضائل، ولما فيها من سعادة البشرية دنيا وديناً، مع يسرها وعدم الحرج
(1) سورة المائدة . آية رقم ٤٨ .

المقتصد، ومنهم المتعمق، والمشقة فيها، لذلك كانت خالدة خلود الدهر، لا تبديل فيها، ولا تحريف إلى أن تقوم الساعة، فكانت رحمة للعالمين وعامة للناس أجمعين، وصدق الله حيث يقول {اليوم أكملت لكم دينكم وأتممت عليكم نعمتي ورضيت لكم الإسلام ديناً} (1) هذا ولما كان علم التوحيد، ويسمى علم الكلام، له هذه المنزلة العظيمة في تأصيل هذه العقيدة والدفاع عنها، عني المتكلمون قديماً وحديثاً بالتأليف فيه، وتباروا في ذلك، فمنهم ومنهم المتوسط. وكان من أشهر الكتب المتعمقة والمشتملة على الأمور العامة التي يحتاج إليها المستدل على حدوث العالم ومنه على وجود الصانع. كتاب المطالب العالية للفخر الرازي والعقائد النسفية للنسفي وكتاب (المواقف) للإيجي شيخ سعد التفتازاني، وكتاب (طوالع الأنوار) للبيضاوي وكتاب (المقاصد) للعلامة السعد التفتازاني، وهو كتاب جامع يحتاج إليه كل باحث، لما حواه من المباحث والنظريات العقلية، وقد تدارك فيه ما فات من كتب من سبقه خاصة كتاب (المواقف) و (المطالب العالية)، وهو وإن كان صعب المنال لدقة أسلوبه وتعمق في أبحاثه، إلا أنه ألف في عصر نضجت فيه العقول، واتسعت مداركها، حتى كانوا لا يقبلون إلا على ما فيه عمق في التفكير والنظر هذا كان دأب المؤلفين في هذا العصر، وشأن تلاميذتهم، فأقدرهم علماً، أعقدهم كتابة. وفي الحق إن الإنسان إذا استسهل الصعب وفكر فيه ونظر، ثم أشحذ ذهنه في المحصل من وراء ذلك على فهم ما دقّ من المسائل، رسخ ذلك في عقله، وربى عنده ملكة قوية، يفهم بها كل ما دق فهمه ولا كذلك الذي يجري وراء السهل من الكتب، فإنه لا تكون له هذه الملكة، ولا تبرز له شخصية يتميز بها عن غيره في الفهم والتحصيل.
ولقد كان كتاب المقاصد من أعقد العقد، حتى تبارى الباحثون في فهمه فكثرت شراحه ليقربوه إلى الأفهام، وكان هذا الكتاب يدرس في الأزهر هو وغيره من الكتب المطولة العميقة، حينما كان هناك علماء، لا يشغل بالهم إلا (1) سورة المائدة آية رقم 3
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Praise be to Allah, the One, the Unique, the Eternal Absolute, who has not taken a companion nor a child, and none shares in His sovereignty. O He whose names are exalted and whose attributes are sanctified. You give and withhold; there is none who can withhold what You give nor give what You withhold. O Owner of Sovereignty, You give sovereignty to whom You will and take it away from whom You will. And prayers and peace be upon the one You chose from sovereignty for the best message, and You revealed to him the best Book for the best nation brought forth to mankind, our master Muhammad ibn Abdullah, the seal of the prophets and messengers, and upon his family and companions and those who follow his path until the Day of Judgment. Now then: The science of tawheed is a science of great status and immense dignity, honored by its relation to Allah, exalted is He, and it is the foundation of every beneficial and useful science. And the creed of the oneness of Allah and His exclusivity in deserving lordship and worship: the command of Allah came with it to every messenger sent to his people to convey to them its adoption; it undergoes no change nor alteration no matter how generations and times change. As for the laws built upon it, they change according to what suits the condition of each nation, in confirmation of His statement, the Most High: {For each We have appointed a law and a way} (1). And when humanity's maturity was complete and its circle of thought and talents expanded, the final message came, containing a tolerant law for every time and place, due to what it includes of general principles and cardinal virtues, and because of the happiness of humanity in this world and religion, with its ease and lack of hardship. (1) Surah al-Ma'idah, verse 48. The moderate, and among them the profound, and the difficulty therein, therefore it was eternal as long as time endures, no alteration in it nor distortion until the Hour is established, so it was a mercy to the worlds and general for all people. And Allah spoke the truth when He says: {Today I have perfected for you your religion and completed upon you My favor and have approved for you Islam as a religion} (1). Now, since the science of tawheed, also called the science of kalam, has this great status in establishing this creed and defending it, the mutakallimun (theologians) of old and recent times took care to author works on it, and they vied in that; among them are the moderate and among them are the profound. And among the most famous profound books that contain the general matters needed by the one seeking proof for the temporal origination of the world and from that the existence of the Maker are: the book al-Matalib al-'Aliya by al-Fakhr al-Razi, al-'Aqa'id al-Nasafiyya by al-Nasafi, the book al-Mawaqif by al-Iji, the teacher of Sa'd al-Taftazani, the book Tawali' al-Anwar by al-Baydawi, and the book al-Maqasid by the scholar Sa'd al-Taftazani, which is a comprehensive book needed by every researcher, because it contains rational investigations and theories, and it made up for what was missing from the books of his predecessors, especially al-Mawaqif and al-Matalib al-'Aliya. And although it is difficult to access due to the precision of its style and depth of its investigations, yet it was authored in an age when minds had matured and their capabilities had expanded, until they would only accept what had depth in thinking and reflection. That was the practice of authors in this age and the habit of their students: the most knowledgeable among them was the most complex in writing. And indeed, if a person eases the difficult, thinks about it and examines it, then sharpens his mind in obtaining from behind that an understanding of the subtle issues, that becomes firmly rooted in his mind and develops in him a strong faculty by which he understands everything that is subtle in comprehension, unlike the one who pursues easy books, for he does not acquire this faculty nor does a personality emerge by which he is distinguished from others in understanding and attainment. And indeed, the book al-Maqasid was among the most knotty of knots, until researchers vied in understanding it and its commentaries multiplied to bring it closer to understanding, and this book used to be studied in al-Azhar, along with other lengthy and profound books, when there were scholars whose minds were occupied only with (1) Surah al-Ma'idah, verse 3.
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage is an introduction written by a modern editor of Sharh al-Maqasid. It begins with the basmalah and a traditional praise of Allah and the Prophet. The editor then declares that the science of tawhid (Islamic theology) is of great dignity because of its subject matter—Allah—and that it is the foundation of all beneficial knowledge. The creed of tawhid, which affirms Allah's oneness and His exclusive right to lordship and worship, is unchanging, though the legal systems based on it varied among earlier nations. The final revelation of Islam, being the last and most complete, is a tolerant law for all times and places. The editor then links this to the science of kalam (dialectical theology), which has the same subject matter and is used to establish and defend the creed. He mentions that scholars have authored many works on kalam, with varying levels of depth. Among the most profound and comprehensive books are: al-Matalib al-'Aliya by Fakhr al-Din al-Razi, al-'Aqa'id al-Nasafiyya by al-Nasafi, al-Mawaqif by al-Iji, Tawali' al-Anwar by al-Baydawi, and al-Maqasid by Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani. He singles out al-Maqasid as particularly difficult but valuable because it covers rational investigations and fills gaps left by earlier works. The editor then reflects on the pedagogical value of studying difficult books: engaging with challenging texts develops strong intellectual faculties and a distinct scholarly personality, unlike studying only easy works. He notes that al-Maqasid was studied in al-Azhar during a time when scholars were devoted to deep study.

Key Terms
علم التوحيد
عقيدة
شرائع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the Islamic creed itself changes over time or across cultures.
Correction: The passage clearly states that the creed of tawhid undergoes no change or alteration; only the legal systems built upon it may vary.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the status of the science of tawhid?
A) It is a moderate science of limited value.
B) It is a noble science that serves as the foundation for all beneficial knowledge.
C) It is a science that changes with each generation.
D) It is only for advanced scholars.

Key Takeaway
The creed of tawhid is fixed and unchanging, while the laws based on it have varied; Islam is the final, perfect, and eternal law.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You claim to believe in the unchanging creed of tawhid, but have you truly submitted your entire life to Allah's exclusive lordship, or do you still have areas where you follow your own desires or other authority? What specific area of your life are you holding back from Allah's rule?
?
The passage states that the final law (Islam) is perfect and complete. Are you living as if that is true, or do you secretly wish for a different set of rules that would suit your convenience? In what way do you 'pick and choose' parts of the sharia that you follow while ignoring others?
?
The creed is unchanging, but our understanding can deepen. Are you actively seeking to increase your knowledge of tawhid, or are you content with a superficial belief? What will you do this week to strengthen your understanding of Allah's names and attributes?

Method of Learning
intermediate

Key Texts of Kalam and the Value of Difficult Books
The editor lists major works of kalam and argues for the pedagogical value of difficult books.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the major classical works of kalam mentioned by the editor and why studying difficult books like al-Maqasid is beneficial for intellectual development.

Core Idea
Studying challenging texts builds a strong scholarly mind; easy books do not.

In this part of the introduction, the editor highlights that because of the great importance of the science of kalam, scholars have produced many works. He lists some of the most profound and comprehensive classical texts, with special attention to al-Maqasid by Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani. He then argues that engaging with difficult books develops a powerful intellectual faculty and a distinct scholarly personality, unlike relying only on easy books.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage listing key books
Identify the five books mentioned: al-Matalib al-'Aliya, al-'Aqa'id al-Nasafiyya, al-Mawaqif, Tawali' al-Anwar, and al-Maqasid. Note their authors and the editor's description of each.
These are foundational texts in the Ash'ari and Maturidi traditions.
2
Focus on al-Maqasid's description
Notice that the editor describes al-Maqasid as comprehensive, covering rational investigations and filling gaps left by earlier works. He also acknowledges its difficulty.
3
Understand the educational benefit of difficulty
The editor argues that struggling with complex texts trains the mind and develops a strong faculty for understanding subtle issues. Easy books do not produce this effect.
This reflects a pedagogical philosophy.
4
Reflect on the scholarly milieu
The passage notes that al-Maqasid was studied in al-Azhar during a time when scholars were deeply devoted to such texts.

Source Text

بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم
الحمد لله الواحد الأحد، الفرد الصمد الذي لم يتخذ صاحبة ولا ولداً. ولم يشاركه في ملكه أحد يا من تعالت أسماؤك، وتقدست صفاتك. تعطي وتمنع، لا مانع لما أعطيت ولا معطي لما منعت، يا مالك الملك، تعطي تشاء وتنزع ممن تشاء، والصلاة والتسليم على من اصطفيته من الملك لخير رسالة، وأنزلت عليه خير كتاب لخير أمة أخرجت للناس، سيدنا محمد ابن عبد الله، خاتم الأنبياء والمرسلين، وعلى آله وصحبه، ومن سار على نهجه إلى يوم الدين .
وبعد
فإن علم التوحيد، علم جليل الشأن عظيم القدر، شرف بنسبته إلى الله سبحانه تعالى، وهو أساس لكل علم نافع ومفيد .
وعقيدة توحيد الله وانفراده باستحقاق الربوبية والمعبودية، جاء أمر الله بها، لكل رسول بعث إلى قومه ليبلغهم باعتناقها لا يعتريها تغيير، ولا تبديل مهما تغيرت الأجيال والأزمان. أما الشرائع المبنية عليها، فإنها تتغير بما يناسب حال كل أمة مصداقاً لقوله تعالى {لكل جعلنا منكم شرعة ومنهاجا} (1) ولما اكتمل رشد الإنسانية واتسعت دائرة تفكيرها ومواهبها جاءت خاتمة الرسالات، متضمنة شريعة سمحاء لكل زمان ومكان لما اشتملت عليه من المبادىء العامة، وأمهات الفضائل، ولما فيها من سعادة البشرية دنيا وديناً، مع يسرها وعدم الحرج
(1) سورة المائدة . آية رقم ٤٨ .

المقتصد، ومنهم المتعمق، والمشقة فيها، لذلك كانت خالدة خلود الدهر، لا تبديل فيها، ولا تحريف إلى أن تقوم الساعة، فكانت رحمة للعالمين وعامة للناس أجمعين، وصدق الله حيث يقول {اليوم أكملت لكم دينكم وأتممت عليكم نعمتي ورضيت لكم الإسلام ديناً} (1) هذا ولما كان علم التوحيد، ويسمى علم الكلام، له هذه المنزلة العظيمة في تأصيل هذه العقيدة والدفاع عنها، عني المتكلمون قديماً وحديثاً بالتأليف فيه، وتباروا في ذلك، فمنهم ومنهم المتوسط. وكان من أشهر الكتب المتعمقة والمشتملة على الأمور العامة التي يحتاج إليها المستدل على حدوث العالم ومنه على وجود الصانع. كتاب المطالب العالية للفخر الرازي والعقائد النسفية للنسفي وكتاب (المواقف) للإيجي شيخ سعد التفتازاني، وكتاب (طوالع الأنوار) للبيضاوي وكتاب (المقاصد) للعلامة السعد التفتازاني، وهو كتاب جامع يحتاج إليه كل باحث، لما حواه من المباحث والنظريات العقلية، وقد تدارك فيه ما فات من كتب من سبقه خاصة كتاب (المواقف) و (المطالب العالية)، وهو وإن كان صعب المنال لدقة أسلوبه وتعمق في أبحاثه، إلا أنه ألف في عصر نضجت فيه العقول، واتسعت مداركها، حتى كانوا لا يقبلون إلا على ما فيه عمق في التفكير والنظر هذا كان دأب المؤلفين في هذا العصر، وشأن تلاميذتهم، فأقدرهم علماً، أعقدهم كتابة. وفي الحق إن الإنسان إذا استسهل الصعب وفكر فيه ونظر، ثم أشحذ ذهنه في المحصل من وراء ذلك على فهم ما دقّ من المسائل، رسخ ذلك في عقله، وربى عنده ملكة قوية، يفهم بها كل ما دق فهمه ولا كذلك الذي يجري وراء السهل من الكتب، فإنه لا تكون له هذه الملكة، ولا تبرز له شخصية يتميز بها عن غيره في الفهم والتحصيل.
ولقد كان كتاب المقاصد من أعقد العقد، حتى تبارى الباحثون في فهمه فكثرت شراحه ليقربوه إلى الأفهام، وكان هذا الكتاب يدرس في الأزهر هو وغيره من الكتب المطولة العميقة، حينما كان هناك علماء، لا يشغل بالهم إلا (1) سورة المائدة آية رقم 3
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Praise be to Allah, the One, the Unique, the Eternal Absolute, who has not taken a companion nor a child, and none shares in His sovereignty. O He whose names are exalted and whose attributes are sanctified. You give and withhold; there is none who can withhold what You give nor give what You withhold. O Owner of Sovereignty, You give sovereignty to whom You will and take it away from whom You will. And prayers and peace be upon the one You chose from sovereignty for the best message, and You revealed to him the best Book for the best nation brought forth to mankind, our master Muhammad ibn Abdullah, the seal of the prophets and messengers, and upon his family and companions and those who follow his path until the Day of Judgment. Now then: The science of tawheed is a science of great status and immense dignity, honored by its relation to Allah, exalted is He, and it is the foundation of every beneficial and useful science. And the creed of the oneness of Allah and His exclusivity in deserving lordship and worship: the command of Allah came with it to every messenger sent to his people to convey to them its adoption; it undergoes no change nor alteration no matter how generations and times change. As for the laws built upon it, they change according to what suits the condition of each nation, in confirmation of His statement, the Most High: {For each We have appointed a law and a way} (1). And when humanity's maturity was complete and its circle of thought and talents expanded, the final message came, containing a tolerant law for every time and place, due to what it includes of general principles and cardinal virtues, and because of the happiness of humanity in this world and religion, with its ease and lack of hardship. (1) Surah al-Ma'idah, verse 48. The moderate, and among them the profound, and the difficulty therein, therefore it was eternal as long as time endures, no alteration in it nor distortion until the Hour is established, so it was a mercy to the worlds and general for all people. And Allah spoke the truth when He says: {Today I have perfected for you your religion and completed upon you My favor and have approved for you Islam as a religion} (1). Now, since the science of tawheed, also called the science of kalam, has this great status in establishing this creed and defending it, the mutakallimun (theologians) of old and recent times took care to author works on it, and they vied in that; among them are the moderate and among them are the profound. And among the most famous profound books that contain the general matters needed by the one seeking proof for the temporal origination of the world and from that the existence of the Maker are: the book al-Matalib al-'Aliya by al-Fakhr al-Razi, al-'Aqa'id al-Nasafiyya by al-Nasafi, the book al-Mawaqif by al-Iji, the teacher of Sa'd al-Taftazani, the book Tawali' al-Anwar by al-Baydawi, and the book al-Maqasid by the scholar Sa'd al-Taftazani, which is a comprehensive book needed by every researcher, because it contains rational investigations and theories, and it made up for what was missing from the books of his predecessors, especially al-Mawaqif and al-Matalib al-'Aliya. And although it is difficult to access due to the precision of its style and depth of its investigations, yet it was authored in an age when minds had matured and their capabilities had expanded, until they would only accept what had depth in thinking and reflection. That was the practice of authors in this age and the habit of their students: the most knowledgeable among them was the most complex in writing. And indeed, if a person eases the difficult, thinks about it and examines it, then sharpens his mind in obtaining from behind that an understanding of the subtle issues, that becomes firmly rooted in his mind and develops in him a strong faculty by which he understands everything that is subtle in comprehension, unlike the one who pursues easy books, for he does not acquire this faculty nor does a personality emerge by which he is distinguished from others in understanding and attainment. And indeed, the book al-Maqasid was among the most knotty of knots, until researchers vied in understanding it and its commentaries multiplied to bring it closer to understanding, and this book used to be studied in al-Azhar, along with other lengthy and profound books, when there were scholars whose minds were occupied only with (1) Surah al-Ma'idah, verse 3.
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage is an introduction written by a modern editor of Sharh al-Maqasid. It begins with the basmalah and a traditional praise of Allah and the Prophet. The editor then declares that the science of tawhid (Islamic theology) is of great dignity because of its subject matter—Allah—and that it is the foundation of all beneficial knowledge. The creed of tawhid, which affirms Allah's oneness and His exclusive right to lordship and worship, is unchanging, though the legal systems based on it varied among earlier nations. The final revelation of Islam, being the last and most complete, is a tolerant law for all times and places. The editor then links this to the science of kalam (dialectical theology), which has the same subject matter and is used to establish and defend the creed. He mentions that scholars have authored many works on kalam, with varying levels of depth. Among the most profound and comprehensive books are: al-Matalib al-'Aliya by Fakhr al-Din al-Razi, al-'Aqa'id al-Nasafiyya by al-Nasafi, al-Mawaqif by al-Iji, Tawali' al-Anwar by al-Baydawi, and al-Maqasid by Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani. He singles out al-Maqasid as particularly difficult but valuable because it covers rational investigations and fills gaps left by earlier works. The editor then reflects on the pedagogical value of studying difficult books: engaging with challenging texts develops strong intellectual faculties and a distinct scholarly personality, unlike studying only easy works. He notes that al-Maqasid was studied in al-Azhar during a time when scholars were devoted to deep study.

السعد التفتازاني
الفخر الرازي

الإيجي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That difficult books are not useful or should be avoided because they are hard to understand.
Correction: The editor argues that difficulty itself is beneficial: it sharpens the mind, builds a strong faculty, and forms a distinct scholarly personality.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which book is described as 'جامع' (comprehensive) and compensates for deficiencies in earlier works?
A) al-Matalib al-'Aliya
B) al-Mawaqif
C) al-Maqasid
D) Tawali' al-Anwar

Key Takeaway
The major works of kalam, especially al-Maqasid, are valuable not only for their content but also for the intellectual discipline gained from studying them.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read a book like al-Maqasid—difficult, dense, demanding—do you press into the discomfort or turn to something easier? What does your answer reveal about your hunger for real knowledge of Allah?
?
You deeply know that you will be asked about your learning on the Day of Judgment. If your study consists only of easy, shallow books, will you be able to say you truly sought the truth with all your ability, or did you settle for comfort?
?
The editor says the most knowledgeable among them was the most complex in writing. Which are you more afraid of: being misunderstood because your words are deep, or being exposed because your knowledge is shallow?

Historical Evolution of Kalam Teaching in al-Azhar
Historical narrative of kalam teaching in al-Azhar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the historical trajectory of teaching advanced kalam texts at al-Azhar, including the shift to easier texts, the later revival, and the eventual decline and decision to reprint.

Core Idea
The teaching of kalam in al-Azhar has seen cycles of depth and simplification.

This passage recounts the fascinating history of how advanced kalam works like al-Mawaqif and al-Maqasid were taught in al-Azhar. It traces the shift from dedicated scholarship to job-oriented learning, leading to the replacement of these texts with simpler summaries. The narrative culminates in a modern initiative to revive these heritage texts. Understanding this history helps us appreciate the value of the book we are studying and its place in the Islamic scholarly tradition.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify key events
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Identify the major turning points: the early period, the 1911 law, the return, the decline, and the revival.
Pay attention to the author's perspective on the motivations of students.
2
Analyze the cause and effect of the 1911 law
Notice how the al-Azhar law replaced complex books with easier ones. Consider why such a change was made and what it reveals about educational reform.
The law is known as Nizam Sheikh Shakir.
3
Reflect on the decline and revival
The passage describes how students later struggled with these books due to job-seeking, leading to reliance on notes and forgetting the books. Then the Committee for Heritage Revival reprinted them. Think about the importance of preserving classical texts.
This directly relates to the purpose of the course you are studying.

الاطلاع على مثل هذه الكتب، وحينما كان هناك أيضاً طلاب يسيرون على منهج أساتذهم، لا يتعلمون إلا للعلم، لا يبغون به جاهاً، ولا مالاً ولا سلطاناً، . واستمر تدريس هذه الكتب في الأزهر إلى أن أنشىء قانون الأزهر الجديد عام ۱۹۱۱م المعروف بنظام الشيخ شاكر، فغيرت هذه الكتب بكتب سهلة التحصيل لأي طالب مثل كتاب (الجوهرة) و (الخريدة) و (أم البراهين) و(المسايرة) وغير ذلك . ولما أنشئت الكليات الأزهرية، رجع الأزهر إلى تدريس بعض هذه الكتب المعقدة، ومنها كتاب المواقف والمقاصد خاصة في نظام التخصص القديم ثم وفي تخصص المادة، حتى تخرج فيها علماء أجلاء يفخر بهم الأزهر، بيد أنه لما كثرت الشواغل وتعلم الطلاب لأجل الوظيفة، صعب عليهم فهم هذه الكتب، فطلبوا من أساتذهم وضع مذكرات ليسهل لهم المرور بها في الامتحان حتى نسوا أسماء هذه الكتب، وأصبح من النادر وجودها لمن يطلبها، لذلك رأت لجنة إحياء التراث المنبثقة من مجمع البحوث الإسلامية، تجديد طبع هذه الكتب، حفاظاً على تراث هؤلاء الأعلام الذين ألفوها حتى كانت مفخرة لهم وللأجيال من بعدهم.
The perusal of such books, and at that time there were also students following the methodology of their teachers, learning only for knowledge, not seeking through it status, nor wealth, nor authority. And the teaching of these books continued in Al-Azhar until the new Al-Azhar law was enacted in 1911 AD, known as the system of Sheikh Shakir, so these books were replaced by books easily taught to any student, such as the book (Al-Jawhara), (Al-Kharida), (Umm Al-Barahin), and (Al-Musayara), and others. And when the Azhari colleges were established, Al-Azhar returned to teaching some of these complex books, among them the book Al-Mawaqif and Al-Maqasid especially in the old specialization system and then in subject specialization, until eminent scholars graduated in them of whom Al-Azhar boasts. But when preoccupations increased and students learned for the sake of employment, understanding these books became difficult for them, so they asked their professors to prepare notes to facilitate their passing the exam until they forgot the names of these books, and their availability became rare for those who seek them. Therefore, the Committee for the Revival of Heritage, emanating from the Islamic Research Academy, decided to reprint these books, preserving the heritage of these great scholars who authored them until they were a pride for them and for the generations after them.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage is a narrative account of the teaching of advanced kalam works in al-Azhar. It first mentions that students studied such books purely for knowledge, not for status or money. Then it notes that teaching continued until the al-Azhar law of 1911 (known as Sheikh Shakir's system) replaced these advanced books with easier texts like al-Jawhara, al-Kharida, Umm al-Barahin, and al-Musayara. Later, when the Azhar colleges were established, the institution returned to teaching some of these complex books, particularly al-Mawaqif and al-Maqasid, especially in the old specialization system and later in subject specialization, producing eminent scholars. However, due to increasing worldly concerns and students' motivation for jobs, these books became difficult for them, so they asked professors for notes to pass exams, ultimately forgetting the books' names and making them rare. Consequently, the Committee for Heritage Revival from the Islamic Research Academy decided to reprint these books to preserve the legacy of their authors. This passage traces the rise, decline, and revival of these Kalam texts in the educational system of al-Azhar.

Correction: This passage shows that they were replaced by easier texts after the 1911 law and later revived, then declined again.

Key Takeaway
This passage shows that the teaching of advanced kalam in al-Azhar went through phases of deep study, replacement by easier texts, return, decline due to utilitarian motives, and finally revival through reprinting efforts.

Editorial Methodology of Dr. Abd al-Rahman Umayra
Describes the editor's methodology: manuscript use, comparison, selection, grammatical correction, title addition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the systematic methodology used by Dr. Abd al-Rahman Umayra in editing al-Maqasid, including manuscript comparison, selection, grammatical purification, and title addition.

Core Idea
Editing is a scholarly science: comparing manuscripts, selecting readings, correcting errors, and adding structure.

This lesson takes you behind the scenes of a critical edition. Dr. Abd al-Rahman Umayra’s methodology reveals the meticulous effort required to produce a reliable text. By examining his approach to al-Maqasid, we gain insight into the scholarly discipline of tahqiq.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once silently, then aloud. Focus on the sequence of actions described by the editor.
Notice the editor’s progression from identifying manuscripts to final textual purification.
2
Identify the five editorial steps
List the key editorial actions mentioned: finding five manuscripts, designating them with letters, comparing copies, giving preference to certain readings with reasons, correcting grammatical errors, and adding titles to untitled sections.
3
Reflect on the significance
Consider why each step matters for producing a trustworthy edition. How does this process differ from simple copying?
This connects to the common misunderstanding that editing is merely copying.

وبالاطلاع على منهج المحقق في تحقيقه لهذا الكتاب، يتضح لنا أيضاً شخصيته الفذة ومدى ما عاناه من جهد وفكر وبعد نظر، حتى جاء التحقيق وافياً للغرض يستفيد منه كل باحث فإنه بعد أن عرف سعد الدين، ومكانته العلمية التي جعلت منه إماماً في المعقول والمنقول، وحافظاً على كتاب الله وسنة رسوله ، وداحضاً لشبه الملحدين والمارقين بالحجة والبرهان وبمثل السلاح الذي تسلح به هؤلاء، سلاح المنطق والعقل، وبعد أن بين ما احتواه الكتاب من مقاصده الست وفصول كل مقصد بعد هذا شرع يبين الخطة التي سار عليها في هذا التحقيق، فبين أنه عثر على خمس نسخ مخطوطة، رمز إلى كل واحدة منها يحرف ، ثم وازن بين هذه النسخ ، ورجح ما اختاره منها للاعتماد عليها مع بيان سبب الترجيح ، ثم عني بتنقية النص من الأخطاء النحوية، وقد رأى أن كثيراً من المباحث والفصول لم يكن لها عنوان، فوضع المحقق العنوان
And by looking at the editor's methodology in his edition of this book, his unique personality also becomes clear to us, and the extent of what he endured of effort, thought, and far-sightedness, until the edition came out complete for the purpose, benefiting every researcher. For after he introduced Sa'd al-Din and his scholarly status that made him an imam in both rational and transmitted sciences, a preserver of the Book of God and the Sunnah of His Messenger, and a refuter of the doubts of atheists and deviants by proof and demonstration and with the same weapon with which these armed themselves – the weapon of logic and reason – and after he explained what the book contained of its six objectives and the chapters of each objective, after this he proceeded to explain the plan he followed in this edition. He explained that he found five manuscript copies, designated each of them with a letter, then compared these copies, and gave preference to what he chose from them for reliance, stating the reason for the preference. Then he attended to purifying the text from grammatical errors, and he saw that many of the sections and chapters had no title, so the editor supplied the title.
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage explains the methodology of the editor, Dr. Abd al-Rahman Umayra. The reviewer states that by examining the editor's approach to this book, one sees his unique personality and the immense effort, thought, and foresight he exerted, resulting in an edition that is comprehensive and beneficial for every researcher. The editor first introduced Sa'd al-Din (the author of al-Maqasid) and his scholarly status, describing him as an imam in both rational and transmitted sciences, a preserver of the Quran and Sunnah, and a refuter of atheists and deviants using proof and demonstration with the same weapons they used: logic and reason. Then the editor explained the six major objectives (maqasid) of the book and the chapters of each objective. After that, he proceeded to outline his editorial plan. The plan includes: he found five manuscript copies, each of which he designated by a letter (or symbol); he compared these copies and gave preference to certain readings, stating the reasons for his choices; he purified the text from grammatical errors; and he noted that many sections and chapters lacked titles, so he supplied titles for them.

Editor's Methodology for Critical Edition
Editor describes his critical edition methodology.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the comprehensive methodology used by the editor of Sharh al-Maqasid in preparing its critical edition.

Core Idea
Critical edition is a scholarly reconstruction, not mere copying.

The editor's methodology reveals the painstaking work behind a reliable critical edition. This lesson outlines the steps he took, from comparing manuscripts to annotating sources. Understanding this process helps us appreciate the trustworthiness of the edition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the editor's preliminary work
Notice how the editor first introduced the author and then explained his plan. This sets the context for the editorial choices.
2
Trace the manuscript comparison process
The editor found five copies, assigned letters, compared, and selected the best. This is the core of textual criticism.
The editor explained the reason for his preference.
3
Observe the supplementary annotations
Beyond cleaning the text, the editor added titles, traced quotations, vocalized Quranic verses, authenticated hadiths, and identified terms and places. These enhancements increase the edition's utility.
He also corrected distortions in quotations by referring to original sources.

وبالاطلاع على منهج المحقق في تحقيقه لهذا الكتاب، يتضح لنا أيضاً شخصيته الفذة ومدى ما عاناه من جهد وفكر وبعد نظر، حتى جاء التحقيق وافياً للغرض يستفيد منه كل باحث فإنه بعد أن عرف سعد الدين، ومكانته العلمية التي جعلت منه إماماً في المعقول والمنقول، وحافظاً على كتاب الله وسنة رسوله ، وداحضاً لشبه الملحدين والمارقين بالحجة والبرهان وبمثل السلاح الذي تسلح به هؤلاء، سلاح المنطق والعقل، وبعد أن بين ما احتواه الكتاب من مقاصده الست وفصول كل مقصد بعد هذا شر شرع يبين الخطة التي سار عليها في هذا التحقيق، فبين أنه عثر على خمس نسخ مخطوطة، رمز إلى كل واحدة منها يحرف ، ثم وازن بين هذه النسخ ، ورجح ما اختاره منها للاعتماد عليها مع بيان سبب الترجيح ، ثم عني بتنقية النص من الأخطاء النحوية، وقد رأى أن كثيراً من المباحث والفصول لم يكن لها عنوان، فوضع المحقق العنوان لها. كما رأى أن السعد في مقاصده ينقل كثيراً من كتاب المواقف، ومن المطالب العالية، ومن كتاب الشفاء ،والنجاة ،والقانون، لابن سينا وغير ذلك، وأنه تارة ينقلها بالمعنى، وتارة يزيد أو ينقص منها. وفي بعض هذه النقول تحريفات، فكان من جهد المحقق أن يرجع إلى النص الأصلي مشيراً إلى تحديد صفحات وأسماء الكتب. كذلك مما عني به المحقق تشكيل الآيات القرآنية، والدلالة على سورها مع ترقيم الآيات. كما عني أيضاً يتخريج الأحاديث التي استشهد بها السعد تخريجاً وافياً من الكتب المعتمدة، وقد عرف البلدان والأماكن التي وردت في كتاب المقاصد، كما عرف المصطلحات العلمية التي ذكرها السعد في كتابه إلى غير ذلك مما جاء في التحقيق. الأمر الذي يدل على جهد المحقق وطول باعه وعمق تفكيره.
By examining the editor's methodology in his edition of this book, his exceptional personality also becomes clear to us, as well as the extent of the effort, thought, and foresight he endured, until the edition came out complete for the purpose, benefiting every researcher. For after he introduced Sa'd al-Din and his scholarly status that made him an imam in the rational and transmitted sciences, a guardian of the Book of Allah and the Sunnah of His Messenger, and a refuter of the doubts of atheists and deviants with proof and evidence and with the same weapon they armed themselves with—the weapon of logic and reason—and after he explained what the book contains of its six purposes and the chapters of each purpose, after this he began to explain the plan he followed in this edition. He showed that he came across five manuscript copies, he assigned a letter to each, then he compared these copies, and preferred what he selected from them for reliance, explaining the reason for preference. Then he undertook to purify the text from grammatical errors, and he saw that many of the topics and chapters had no title, so he placed titles for them. He also saw that al-Sa'd in his Maqasid frequently quotes from the book al-Mawaqif, and from al-Matalib al-'Aliya, and from the books al-Shifa', al-Najat, and al-Qanun by Ibn Sina and others, and that sometimes he quotes them by meaning, and sometimes he adds or subtracts from them. In some of these quotations there are distortions, so it was among the editor's efforts to refer back to the original text, indicating the pages and names of the books. Likewise, among what the editor attended to was vocalizing the Qur'anic verses, indicating their surahs with verse numbering. He also attended to the complete authentication of the hadiths that al-Sa'd cited from reliable books. He identified the countries and places mentioned in the book al-Maqasid, and he identified the scientific terms that al-Sa'd mentioned in his book, and other things that came in the edition. This indicates the editor's effort, extensive knowledge, and depth of thought.
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage is a methodological description of the editor's work on the critical edition of Sharh al-Maqasid. It begins by praising the editor's character and effort, then outlines the editor's approach step by step. First, the editor introduces the author, Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani, highlighting his status as an imam in both rational and transmitted sciences, a defender of orthodoxy using logic and reason. Then the editor explains his own editorial plan: he found five manuscript copies and assigned a letter to each for identification. He compared these copies and selected the best one, justifying his preference. He cleaned the text of grammatical errors and added titles to untitled sections. He noticed that al-Taftazani often quotes from earlier works like al-Mawaqif, al-Matalib al-'Aliya, and works by Ibn Sina, sometimes paraphrasing or altering the text, and these quotations contained distortions, so the editor traced the original sources with page references. Additionally, the editor vocalized Qur'anic verses, indicated their surahs and verse numbers, fully authenticated the hadiths cited, identified geographical places, and defined technical terms. This comprehensive work demonstrates the editor's deep knowledge and diligence.

Correction: It involves collation, comparison, emendation, and extensive annotation to produce a reliable text.

The Quran as Foundation of Kalam
Author argues the Quran is a primary source for kalam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Quran is considered a foundational factor in the emergence of 'ilm al-kalam, based on the arguments of classical scholars.

Core Idea
The Quran itself is the primary source of rational proofs for kalam.

This passage addresses a common misconception that 'ilm al-kalam is foreign to the Quran. The author argues that the Quran is not only compatible with rational theology but is its very source. He cites three authorities to show that the Quran contains the seeds of theological reasoning, and that early Muslims deduced their methods from it.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the overall argument. Notice how the author poses a question and then cites authorities.
2
Examine al-Qushayri's quote
Identify the astonishment of al-Qushayri at those who deny kalam in the Quran. He points out that verses on principles (usul) far outnumber legal verses.
This shows the Quran's emphasis on foundational beliefs.
3
Examine al-Zarkashi's quote
Al-Zarkashi states that all rational and revealed knowledge is in the Quran, but presented in Arab custom, not technical terms. He adds that rational proofs can be deduced from it.
This addresses the style of the Quran as accessible yet profound.
4
Examine Dr. Dunya's assertion
Dr. Sulayman Dunya affirms the Quran's foundational role and rejects the claim that it hinders rational thought.
This concludes the argument against the misconception.
5
Synthesize the evidence
Consider how these three citations collectively support the claim that the Quran is a primary factor in the emergence of kalam.
The argument moves from specific examples to a general conclusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقبل الإجابة على ذلك، نتساءل كيف نشأ علم الكلام في حياة المسلمين . . ؟ أعني ما هي العوامل التي ساعدت على إيجاده، ومازالت به حتى أصلته، ووضعت له المبادىء والقواعد الأساسية..؟ وإذا كان هذا العلم لم يعرف في البيئة العربية، قبل ظهور الإسلام، وقبل مبعث الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم أيكون القرآن الكريم وما فيه من أدلة قاطعة وبراهين ساطعة، هو أحد العوامل الأساسية في إنشاء علم الكلام؟ إن ابن عساكر في كتبه تبيين كذب المفتري يروي عن الإمام القشيري قوله : «والعجب ممن يقول : ليس في القرآن علم الكلام. والآيات التي هي في الأحكام الشرعية نجدها محصورة، والآيات المنبهة على علم الأصول نجدها توفي على ذلك، وتربى بكثير من الزيادة (1) . ويقول صاحب البرهان : وما من برهان ودلالة وتقسيم وتحديد شيء من كليات المعلومات العقلية والسمعية إلا كتاب الله تعالى قد نطق به. لكن أورده تعالى على عادة العرب، دون دقائق طرق أحكام المتكلمين». ثم يقول : واعلم أنه قد يظهر منه بدقيق الفكر استنباط البراهين العقلية، على طرق المتلكمين» (۲). والدكتور سليمان دنيا يقرر أن الدور الأساسي في نشأة علم الكلام كان للقرآن وينكر بقوة دعوى البعض أن القرآن يعوق النظر العقلي (۳)
Before answering that, we ask: how did 'ilm al-kalam originate in the life of Muslims? I mean, what factors helped bring it into existence, continued with it until it was established, and laid down its basic principles and rules? And if this science was not known in the Arab environment before the advent of Islam and before the mission of the Prophet (peace be upon him), is the Noble Quran, with its decisive proofs and brilliant evidences, one of the fundamental factors in the establishment of 'ilm al-kalam? Ibn 'Asakir in his book Tabyin Kadhib al-Muftari narrates from Imam al-Qushayri his statement: 'It is astonishing that someone says there is no 'ilm al-kalam in the Quran. The verses on legal rulings are limited, but the verses pointing to the science of principles (usul) we find exceed that and are much more numerous.' And the author of al-Burhan says: 'There is no proof, evidence, division, or definition of any universal of rational or revealed knowledge except that the Book of God has spoken of it. But God presented it according to the Arab custom, without the subtle methods of the theologians.' Then he says: 'Know that from it, with precise thought, one can deduce rational proofs according to the methods of the theologians.' And Dr. Sulayman Dunya affirms that the fundamental role in the emergence of 'ilm al-kalam belonged to the Quran, and he strongly denies the claim of some that the Quran hinders rational thought.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage is an argument for the Quran as a primary source of 'ilm al-kalam. The author begins by posing the question of how kalam arose, noting that the Quran contains decisive proofs. He then cites three authorities: al-Qushayri, who marvels at those who deny kalam in the Quran and points out that verses on usul (principles) far outnumber legal verses; al-Zarkashi (author of al-Burhan), who states that all rational and revealed knowledge is present in the Quran but in the Arab style, not the technical terminology of theologians; and Dr. Sulayman Dunya, who affirms the Quran's foundational role and rejects the claim that it hinders reason. Thus, the passage establishes that the Quran is not an obstacle but an impetus for theological reflection.

Correction: The passage shows that the Quran is the very source of rational proofs and does not hinder reason.

Key Takeaway
The Quran is the foundational source of rational proofs in 'ilm al-kalam, contrary to claims that it hinders reason.

What would it mean for you to trust that the Quran contains all rational knowledge, even if expressed in Arab custom?

The Quran and Hadith as Foundational Sources of Kalam
The author presents the Quran and a hadith about whispered thoughts as factors in the rise of ilm al-kalam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quran and hadith served as primary factors in the emergence of ilm al-kalam, and how early theological questions were addressed within the Islamic tradition.

Core Idea
Kalam is rooted in the Quran and hadith, not a foreign innovation.

The author argues that ilm al-kalam emerged from within Islam, not from external influences. He points to the Quran as a fundamental factor and to a key hadith that shows the Prophet himself addressed theological questions. This passage establishes that the seeds of kalam were planted in the earliest Islamic sources.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice the author's rhetorical question and his citation of a hadith.
2
Analyze the argument structure
Identify the author's claim: the Quran and hadith were factors in kalam's emergence. Notice he uses a hadith as evidence. How does the hadith illustrate early theological inquiry?
The hadith shows the Companions struggled with questions about creation and the Creator.
3
Reflect on the significance
Consider why this argument matters. It counters the idea that kalam is a foreign discipline. The Prophet's response shows that pondering such questions is part of faith, not its opposite.
The Prophet called these thoughts 'clear faith' (صريح الإيمان).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فهل نرى أن القرآن كان أحد العوامل الأساسية في نشأة علم الكلام؟ إن بعض العلماء يقرر ذلك، ويضيف إليه أن أحاديث الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم كانت عاملاً مساعداً في إيجاد علم الكلام من ذلك أن الإمام البغوي ذكر حديثاً من الصحاح بسنده عن أبي هريرة رضي الله عنه أنه قال :
جاء ناس من أصحاب رسول الله إلى النبي فسألوه. إنا نجد في أنفسنا ما يتعاظم أحدنا أن يتكلم به .
كذا؟
قال : أوجدتموه؟
قالوا: نعم.
قال : ذاك صريح الإيمان وقال : يأتي الشيطان أحدكم فيقول : من خلق خلق كذا؟ حتى يقول : من خلق ربك فإذا بلغه فليستعذ بالله ولينته . من وقال: «لا يزال الناس يتساءلون حتى يقال : هذا الله خلق الخلق فمن خلق الله ؟ فمن وجد مثل ذلك شيئاً فليقل: آمنت بالله ورسوله» (۱).
So do we see that the Quran was one of the fundamental factors in the emergence of ilm al-kalam? Some scholars affirm that, and add to it that the hadiths of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) were a contributing factor in the creation of ilm al-kalam. From that, Imam al-Baghawi mentioned a hadith from the authentic collections with his chain from Abu Huraira (may Allah be pleased with him) that he said: 'People from the Companions of the Messenger of Allah came to the Prophet and asked him: "We find within ourselves that which one of us would consider too grave to speak of." He said: "Do you find it?" They said: "Yes." He said: "That is clear faith." And he said: "Satan comes to one of you and says: 'Who created such and such?' until he says: 'Who created your Lord?' So when he reaches that, let him seek refuge in Allah and desist." And he said: "People will keep asking until it is said: 'Allah created the creation, so who created Allah?' Whoever finds something like that, let him say: 'I believe in Allah and His Messenger.'" (1)'
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage presents the first set of evidence for the Islamic origins of ilm al-kalam. The author begins by asking whether the Quran was a fundamental factor, then affirms that some scholars hold this view and add the hadith as a supporting factor. The hadith from Abu Huraira illustrates that even the Companions experienced troubling thoughts about creation and the Creator. The Prophet's response — instructing them to seek refuge in Allah and affirm faith — shows that such theological questions were addressed from the earliest period. The author uses this to argue that kalam is rooted in the primary sources of Islam, not a foreign innovation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Early Incidents of Theological Questioning
Narrative of two early theological incidents as precursors to kalam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand two early incidents where individuals questioned the Quran and how the responses of Caliph Umar and Ali are cited as factors in the emergence of ilm al-kalam.

Core Idea
Early suppression of theological questions paradoxically spurred the development of kalam.

This passage from Sharh al-Maqasid recounts two episodes from the caliphates of Umar and Ali. In the first, a man named Sabigh asks about ambiguous Quranic verses and is severely punished. In the second, a man asks whether the Quran is created, and Ali threatens execution. The author then asks whether such internal Muslim tensions contributed to the rise of kalam. Let's examine these stories and the author's framing.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that it begins by describing the state of Muslims after the Prophet's death, then narrates two specific incidents.
The text ends abruptly mid-sentence.
2
Analyze the Sabigh incident
Focus on the story of Sabigh. What was his question? How did Umar respond? What does this show about early attitudes toward theological inquiry?
Umar used physical punishment and social boycott.
3
Analyze the creation of Quran incident
Look at the second incident: a man asks about the createdness of the Quran. What did Ali say? How does this reflect the gravity of the issue?
Ali's threat of execution shows the potential danger of such questions.
4
Reflect on the author's question
The author asks whether these internal factors led to kalam or if other reasons were involved. Consider your own view before the text cuts off.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم ماذا؟ لقد مات الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم ، والمسلمون أمرهم جميع، يعرفون دينهم، وينفذون تعاليم ربهم - غير هنات صغيرة .. وفي عهد أبي بكر رضي الله عنه انشغل المسلمون بحروب الردة، وجاء عهد عمر بن الخطاب رضي الله عنه، فقدم عليه رجل يقال له (صبيغ) فجعل يسأل عن متشابه القرآن - فأرسل إليه عمر ـ وقد أعد له عراجين النخل، فلما قال له عمر من أنت؟ قال : أنا عبد الله صبيغ ، فأخذ عرجوناً من تلك العراجين فضربه حتى أدمى رأسه، ثم عادله ثم تركه حتى برأ. فدعا به ليعود فقال : إن كنت تريد قتلي، فاقتلني قتلاً جميلاً . فأذن له إلى أرضه، وكتب إلى أبي موسى الأشعري ألا يجالسه أحد من المسلمين. وأخرج نصر المقدسي وابن عساكر عن أبي عثمان النهدي. أن عمر كتب إلى أهل البصرة ألا يجالسوا صبيغاً ولا يبايعوه، وإن مرض فلا يعودوه، وإن مات فلا يشهدوه (۱) ؟ ) . وأخرج نصر أيضاً عن أبي هريرة رضي الله عنه قال: كنا عند عمر بن الخطاب رضي الله عنه. إذ جاءه رجل يسأله عن القرآن. أمخلوق هو أو غير مخلوق؟ . فقال علي رضي الله عنه : هذه كلمة وسيكون لها ثمرة، ولو وليت من الأمر ما ولیت، ضربت عنقه . . أتكون هذه الوسائل والخطرات التي كانت تهجس في داخل بعض النفوس، لها دخل في إنشاء علم الكلام ..؟ أو أن وراء إنشائه وإيجاده أسباباً أخرى، مع التي ذكرنا، دفعت المسلمين إلى طريق الجدل، واصطناع علم الكلام .. ؟ إننا نرى ويشاركنا في رأينا هذا كثير من العلماء أن تطلع بعض المسلمين
Then what? The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) died, and the Muslims were united in their affair, knowing their religion, and executing the teachings of their Lord – except for minor flaws. And in the era of Abu Bakr (may Allah be pleased with him), the Muslims were occupied with the wars of apostasy. Then came the era of 'Umar ibn al-Khattab (may Allah be pleased with him), and a man called (Sabigh) came to him and began asking about the ambiguous verses of the Quran. So 'Umar sent for him – and he had prepared palm branches. When 'Umar said to him: 'Who are you?' He said: 'I am 'Abdullah Sabigh.' So he took a palm branch and struck him until he bloodied his head, then he left him until he recovered. Then he called him again and he said: 'If you want to kill me, kill me beautifully.' So he allowed him to go to his land, and wrote to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari that none of the Muslims should sit with him. And Nasr al-Maqdisi and Ibn 'Asakir narrated from Abu 'Uthman al-Nahdi that 'Umar wrote to the people of Basra: 'Do not sit with Sabigh, do not trade with him, if he is sick do not visit him, and if he dies do not attend his funeral.' (1) And Nasr also narrated from Abu Huraira (may Allah be pleased with him) that he said: We were with 'Umar ibn al-Khattab (may Allah be pleased with him) when a man came to him asking about the Quran: 'Is it created or uncreated?' So 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) said: 'This is a word that will have consequences. If I were in charge of the matter, I would strike his neck.' Could these means and thoughts that were stirring within some souls have had a hand in the establishment of ilm al-kalam? Or are there other reasons, besides those we have mentioned, that drove the Muslims to the path of debate and the creation of ilm al-kalam? Indeed, we see – and many scholars share this view with us – that some Muslims' ... (text cut off).
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage presents post-prophetic historical incidents as further factors leading to ilm al-kalam. The author notes that after the Prophet's death, Muslims were generally united but soon faced challenges. The story of Sabigh, who asked about ambiguous Quranic verses, resulted in severe punishment from 'Umar and social boycott. Similarly, a man asked about whether the Quran is created or uncreated, to which 'Ali responded that such questioning would have grave consequences and that he would execute the questioner. These incidents show that early authorities suppressed certain theological inquiries. The author then asks rhetorically whether these internal thoughts and questions contributed to the establishment of kalam, or whether other reasons drove Muslims to debate and systematic theology. The passage ends mid-sentence, indicating that the author is about to present his own view, but the text is incomplete.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

?
'Ali called the question about the Quran's createdness 'a word that will have consequences.' Have you ever said or believed something that had unintended consequences? How does this incident make you reflect on the weight of your own words in religious matters?

Umar's Response to Sabigh: Early Islamic Attitude to Mutashabih
Story of Sabigh and Umar's harsh response to questioning mutashabih.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the early Islamic attitude toward speculative questioning of ambiguous Quranic verses, as illustrated by the story of Sabigh and Umar.

Core Idea
Questioning ambiguous verses was severely discouraged in early Islam.

This passage recounts a well-known incident from the caliphate of Umar ibn al-Khattab. A man named Sabigh came to Medina and began asking about the ambiguous (mutashabih) verses of the Quran. Umar's response was swift and harsh: he beat Sabigh and then ordered the community to shun him. The story serves as a practical demonstration of how the early Muslim community dealt with theological curiosity that threatened to lead to discord.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and the translation. Notice the sequence of events: Sabigh's questioning, Umar's preparation, the beating, the recovery, the second call, and the final order of social isolation.
Pay attention to the severity of the punishment.
2
Reflect on Umar's actions
Consider why Umar reacted so strongly. The passage suggests that asking about mutashabih was considered dangerous. Umar used both physical punishment and social shunning.
Reflect on the phrase 'قتلاً جميلاً' (a beautiful killing) and the ban on social interaction.
3
Connect to broader principles
Think about how this incident reflects the early Muslim approach to traditional education. They valued practice and certainty over speculative questioning.
This story is often cited to discourage delving into theological debates that distract from practical religion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم ماذا؟ لقد مات الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم ، والمسلمون أمرهم جميع، يعرفون دينهم، وينفذون تعاليم ربهم - غير هنات صغيرة .. وفي عهد أبي بكر رضي الله عنه انشغل المسلمون بحروب الردة، وجاء عهد عمر بن الخطاب رضي الله عنه، فقدم عليه رجل يقال له (صبيغ) فجعل يسأل عن متشابه القرآن - فأرسل إليه عمر ـ وقد أعد له عراجين النخل، فلما قال له عمر من أنت؟ قال : أنا عبد الله صبيغ ، فأخذ عرجوناً من تلك العراجين فضربه حتى أدمى رأسه، ثم عادله ثم تركه حتى برأ. فدعا به ليعود فقال : إن كنت تريد قتلي، فاقتلني قتلاً جميلاً . فأذن له إلى أرضه، وكتب إلى أبي موسى الأشعري ألا يجالسه أحد من المسلمين. وأخرج نصر المقدسي وابن عساكر عن أبي عثمان النهدي. أن عمر كتب إلى أهل البصرة ألا يجالسوا صبيغاً ولا يبايعوه، وإن مرض فلا يعودوه، وإن مات فلا يشهدوه (۱).
Then what? The Messenger of God (peace be upon him) died, and the Muslims were united in their affairs, knowing their religion and implementing the teachings of their Lord—except for small blemishes. During the caliphate of Abu Bakr (may God be pleased with him), the Muslims were occupied with the wars of apostasy. Then came the caliphate of Umar ibn al-Khattab (may God be pleased with him), and a man named (Sabigh) came to him and began asking about the ambiguous parts of the Quran. So Umar sent for him, having prepared palm branches. When Umar said to him, 'Who are you?' He said, 'I am Abdullah Sabigh.' He took a palm branch from those branches and struck him until he made his head bleed, then he left him until he recovered. He called him again and he said, 'If you want to kill me, kill me beautifully.' So he permitted him to go to his land and wrote to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari that none of the Muslims should sit with him. And Nasr al-Maqdisi and Ibn Asakir narrated from Abu Uthman al-Nahdi that Umar wrote to the people of Basra: 'Do not sit with Sabigh, do not trade with him, if he is sick do not visit him, and if he dies do not attend his funeral.' (1)
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage narrates a historical incident to illustrate the early Muslim attitude toward speculative questioning about religious texts. It describes how, after the Prophet's death and the apostasy wars, Umar ibn al-Khattab dealt severely with a man named Sabigh who persistently asked about mutashabih (ambiguous verses) of the Quran. Umar physically punished him, then exiled him socially by instructing others to shun him. The author cites this as evidence that early Muslim authorities discouraged delving into ambiguous theological questions.

Greek and Persian Influence on the Emergence of Ilm al-Kalam
The author discusses external intellectual influences on the rise of kalam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the argument that the translation of Greek and Persian philosophical works was a key factor in the development of ilm al-kalam.

Core Idea
External intellectual heritage shaped the birth of Islamic theology.

The author raises a critical question: were internal Muslim debates alone responsible for the rise of kalam, or were there external influences? He argues that the translation movement brought Greek and Persian thought into the Islamic world, providing tools and concepts that shaped kalam. Some even went further, claiming kalam originated in Greece itself.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the translation. Pay attention to the rhetorical question at the beginning.
Notice the author's use of rhetorical questioning to introduce the topic.
2
Identify the main thesis
Find where the author states his view on the external factor. Look for the phrase 'نرى ويشاركنا في رأينا هذا كثير من العلماء'.
Also note the extreme view that kalam originated in Greece—the author presents it as exaggeration.
3
Reflect on the consequences
Consider the claim that this influence fragmented Islamic thought. The passage ends with the current state of kalam.
Think about how external ideas can both enrich and challenge a tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أتكون هذه الوسائل والخطرات التي كانت تهجس في داخل بعض النفوس، لها دخل في إنشاء علم الكلام ..؟ أو أن وراء إنشائه وإيجاده أسباباً أخرى، مع التي ذكرنا، دفعت المسلمين إلى طريق الجدل، واصطناع علم الكلام .. ؟ إننا نرى ويشاركنا في رأينا هذا كثير من العلماء أن تطلع بعض المسلمين إلى تراث الأمم السابقة كدولة الفرس واليونان وعكوفهم على ترجمة هذه الكتب عامل جوهري أيضاً في تعرف المسلمين على علم الكلام، وحذقهم لأدواته بل يبالغ البعض فيرى أن هذا العلم نبتت جذوره في دولة اليونان، وغذيت فروعه في مدارسه المختلفة من أبيقورية ورواقية، وسفسطائية، ثم زحف على الأمة الإسلامية فيما زحف فكان والحق يقال : لفكرها مشتتاً، ولرأيها مفرقاً، ولوحدتها ممزقاً وبقي إلى يومنا هذا علماً يعرف به من يشتغلون في البحث عن العقائد والملل المختلفة، وممن تستهويهم حقائق الوجود ومغلقات الكون وغير ذلك من الأبحاث الفلسفية.
Could these means and thoughts that were stirring within some souls have had a role in the establishment of ilm al-kalam? Or are there other reasons, besides those we mentioned, that drove Muslims to the path of debate and the creation of ilm al-kalam? We hold—and many scholars share this view—that the exposure of some Muslims to the heritage of previous nations such as the Persians and Greeks, and their dedication to translating these books, was also a fundamental factor in Muslims' acquaintance with ilm al-kalam and their mastery of its tools. Indeed, some go so far as to claim that this science had its roots in Greece, and its branches were nourished in its various schools—Epicurean, Stoic, and Sophist—then it advanced upon the Islamic community, and the truth is that it scattered its thought, divided its opinion, and tore apart its unity. And it remains to this day a science by which are known those who engage in research on doctrines and various sects, and those who are fascinated by the realities of existence, the mysteries of the universe, and other philosophical inquiries.
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage poses a rhetorical question about the origins of ilm al-kalam and presents the view that exposure to Greek and Persian philosophical heritage—through translation movements—was a major factor. The author notes that some even claim the science originated in Greece and spread to Islam, causing disunity. The passage concludes that ilm al-kalam is still used by those studying sects and philosophical questions.

Misconception: The belief that ilm al-kalam originated entirely in Greece and is purely a foreign import.
Correction: The passage presents this as an exaggeration ('بالغ البعض'), and the author's own view is that translation and exposure were important factors, not that kalam is entirely Greek.

The translation of Greek and Persian philosophical works was a crucial external factor in the formation of ilm al-kalam.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
